That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain but\\n474: \\t// cookie/session-based authentication is only allowed if the origin is in the configured\\n475: \\t// allow-list of origins. Otherwise, only access token authentication is permitted.\\n476: \\t//\\n477: \\t// This is to be used for all /.api routes, such as our GraphQL and search streaming APIs as we\\n478: \\t// want third-party websites (such as e.g. github1s.com, or internal tools for on-prem\\n479: \\t// customers) to be able to leverage our API. Their users will need to provide an access token,\\n480: \\t// or the website would need to be added to Sourcegraph's CORS allow list in order to be granted\\n481: \\t// cookie/session-based authentication (which is dangerous to expose to untrusted domains.)\\n482: \\tcrossOriginPolicyAPI crossOriginPolicy = \\\"API\\\"\\n483: \\n484: \\t// crossOriginPolicyAssets describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests to\\n485: \\t// static resources as a public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain.\\n486: \\t//\\n487: \\t// This is to be used for static assets served from the /.assets route. For example, using this\\n488: \\t// route, the Phabricator native extension loads styles via the fetch interface.\\n489: \\tcrossOriginPolicyAssets crossOriginPolicy = \\\"assets\\\"\\n490: \\n491: \\t// crossOriginPolicyNever describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests by\\n492: \\t// never allowing them. This makes sense for e.g. routes such as e.g. sign out pages, where\\n493: \\t// cookie based authentication is needed and requests should never come from a domain other than\\n494: \\t// the Sourcegraph instance itself.\\n495: \\t//\\n496: \\t// Important: This only applies to cross-origin requests issued by clients that respect CORS,\\n497: \\t// such as browsers. So for example Code Intelligence /.executors, despite being \\\"an API\\\",\\n498: \\t// should use this policy unless they intend to get cross-origin requests _from browsers_.\\n499: \\tcrossOriginPolicyNever crossOriginPolicy = \\\"never\\\"\\n500: )\\n501: \\n502: // secureHeadersMiddleware adds and checks for HTTP security-related headers.\\n503: //\\n504: // 🚨 SECURITY: This handler is served to all clients, even on private servers to clients who have\\n505: // not authenticated. It must not reveal any sensitive information.\\n506: func secureHeadersMiddleware(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, next http.Handler, policy crossOriginPolicy) http.Handler {\\n507: \\treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\\n508: \\t\\t// headers for security\\n509: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-Content-Type-Options\\\", \\\"nosniff\\\")\\n510: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-XSS-Protection\\\", \\\"1; mode=block\\\")\\n511: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-Frame-Options\\\", \\\"DENY\\\")\\n512: \\t\\t// no cache by default\\n513: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Cache-Control\\\", \\\"no-cache, max-age=0\\\")\\n514: \\n515: \\t\\t// Write CORS headers and potentially handle the requests if it is an OPTIONS request.\\n516: \\t\\tif handled := handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin(logger, db), w, r, policy); handled {\\n517: \\t\\t\\treturn // request was handled, do not invoke next handler\\n518: \\t\\t}\\n519: \\n520: \\t\\tnext.ServeHTTP(w, r)\\n521: \\t})\\n522: }\\n523: \\n524: // handleCORSRequest handles checking the Origin header and writing CORS Access-Control-Allow-*\\n525: // headers. In some cases, it may handle OPTIONS CORS preflight requests in which case the function\\n526: // returns true and the request should be considered fully served.\\n527: func handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin func(context.Context, string) bool, w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request, policy crossOriginPolicy) (handled bool) {\\n528: \\t// If this route is one which should never allow cross-origin requests, then we should return\\n529: \\t// early. We do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browsers\\n530: \\t// default (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\\n531: \\t//\\n532: \\t// We could instead parse the domain from conf.Get().ExternalURL and use that in the response,\\n533: \\t// to make things more explicit, but it would add more logic here to think about and you would\\n534: \\t// also want to think about whether or not `OPTIONS` requests should be handled and if the other\\n535: \\t// headers (-Credentials, -Methods, -Headers, etc.) should be sent back in such a situation.\\n536: \\t// Instead, it's easier to reason about the code by just saying \\\"we send back nothing in this\\n537: \\t// case, and so the browser enforces no cross-origin requests\\\".\\n538: \\t//\\n539: \\t// This is in compliance with section 7.2 \\\"Resource Sharing Check\\\" of the CORS standard: https://www.w3.org/TR/2020/SPSD-cors-20200602/#resource-sharing-check-0\\n540: \\t// It states:\\n541: \\t//\\n542: \\t// > If the response includes zero or more than one Access-Control-Allow-Origin header values,\\n543: \\t// > return fail and terminate this algorithm.\\n544: \\t//\\n545: \\t// And you may also see the type of error the browser would produce in this instance at e.g.\\n546: \\t// https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Errors/CORSMissingAllowOrigin\\n547: \\t//\\n548: \\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyNever {\\n549: \\t\\treturn false\\n550: \\t}\\n551: \\n552: \\t// If the crossOriginPolicyAssets is used and the requested asset is not from the extension folder,\\n553: \\t// we do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browser's default\\n554: \\t// (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\\n555: \\t//\\n556: \\t// We allow cross-origin requests for assets in the `./client/web/dist/extension` folder because they\\n557: \\t// are required for the native Phabricator extension.\\n558: \\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyAssets && !strings.HasPrefix(r.URL.Path, \\\"/extension/\\\") {\\n559: \\t\\treturn false\\n560: \\t}\\n561: \\n562: \\t// Check Fetch metadata to determine request site, if the request is cross-site\\n563: \\t// or the metadata doesn't exist we handle the request.\\n564: \\tif reqSite := r.Header.Get(csrf.SecFetchSite); reqSite != \\\"\\\" && reqSite != \\\"cross-site\\\" {\\n565: \\t\\treturn false\\n566: \\t}\\n567: \\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI and crossOriginPolicyAssets - handling of API and static assets routes.\\n568: \\t//\\n569: \\t// Even if the request was not from a trusted origin, we will allow the browser to send it AND\\n570: \\t// include credentials even. Traditionally, this would be a CSRF vulnerability! But because we\\n571: \\t// know for a fact that we will only respect sessions (cookie-based-authentication) iff the\\n572: \\t// request came from a trusted origin, in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety, we know it\\n573: \\t// is safe to do this.\\n574: \\t//\\n575: \\t// This is the ONLY way in which we can enable public access of our Sourcegraph.com API, i.e. to\\n576: \\t// allow random.com to send requests to our GraphQL and search APIs either unauthenticated or\\n577: \\t// using an access token.\\n578: \\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Credentials\\\", \\\"true\\\")\\n579: \\n580: \\t// Note: This must mirror the request's `Origin` header exactly as API users rely on this\\n581: \\t// codepath handling for example wildcards `*` and `null` origins properly. For example, if\\n582: \\t// Sourcegraph is behind a corporate VPN an admin may choose to set the CORS origin to \\\"*\\\" (via\\n583: \\t// a proxy, a browser would never send a literal \\\"*\\\") and would expect Sourcegraph to respond\\n584: \\t// appropriately with the request's Origin header. Similarly, some environments issue requests\\n585: \\t// with a `null` Origin header, such as VS Code extensions from within WebViews and Figma\\n586: \\t// extensions. Thus:\\n587: \\t//\\n588: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: *\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\\\"\\n589: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: null\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: null\\\"\\n590: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: https://foobar.com\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://foobar.com\\\"\\n591: \\t//\\n592: \\t// Again, this is fine because we allow API requests from any origin and instead prevent CSRF\\n593: \\t// attacks via enforcing that we only respect session auth iff the origin is trusted. See the\\n594: \\t// docstring above this one for more info.\\n595: \\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin\\\", r.Header.Get(\\\"Origin\\\"))\\n596: \\n597: \\tif r.Method == \\\"OPTIONS\\\" {\\n598: \\t\\t// CRITICAL: Only trusted origins are allowed to send the secure X-Requested-With and\\n599: \\t\\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client headers, which indicate to us later (in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety)\\n600: \\t\\t// that the request came from a trusted origin. It is NOT respected anymore, but is left as an allowed header so as to not block\\n613: \\t\\t\\t// requests that still do include it as e.g. part of a proxy put in front of Sourcegraph.\\n614: \\t\\t\\theaders = append(headers, corsAllowHeader, \\\"X-Sourcegraph-Client\\\")\\n615: \\t\\t}\\n616: \\n617: \\t\\t// Add headers specified by the site config. Importantly, this list does _not_ include\\n635: \\t\\t// corsAllowHeader. The list is formatted for use with Access-Control-Allow-Headers.\\n636: \\t\\t//\\n637: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace: indicates whether we should enable tracing for the request\\n638: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name: contains a client-reported name for the request source. Used for event metadata.\\n640: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature: contains a client reported feature for the request source. Used for event metadata.\\n641: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID: reports an anonymous ID for clients that are not logged in. Used for event metadata unauthed dotcom users.\\n642: \\t\\tconst safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins = \\\"Content-Type, Authorization, X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature, X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID\\\"\\n643: \\t\\theaders = append(headers, safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins)\\n644: \\n645: \\t}\\n649: \\treturn false\\n650: }\\n651: \\n652: // isTrustedOrigin returns whether the HTTP request's Origin is trusted to\\n653: // initiate authenticated cross-origin requests.\\n654: func \\treturn h\\n459: }\\n460: \\n461: // corsAllowHeader is the HTTP header that, if present (and assuming secureHeadersMiddleware is\\n462: // used), indicates that the incoming HTTP request is either same-origin or is from an allowed\\n463: // origin. See\\n464: // https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Cross-Site_Request_Forgery_(CSRF)_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet#Protecting_REST_Services:_Use_of_Custom_Request_Headers\\n465: // for more information on this technique.\\n466: const corsAllowHeader = \\\"X-Requested-With\\\"\\n467: \\n468: // crossOriginPolicy describes the cross-origin policy the middleware should be enforcing.\\n469: type crossOriginPolicy string\\n470: \\n471: const (\\n472: \\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests as a\\n473: \\t// public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain but\\n474: \\t// cookie/session-based authentication is only allowed if the origin is in the configured\\n475: \\t// allow-list of origins. Otherwise, only access token authentication is permitted.\\n476: \\t//\\n477: \\t// This is to be used for all /.api routes, such as our GraphQL and search streaming APIs as we\\n478: \\t// want third-party websites (such as e.g. github1s.com, or internal tools for on-prem\\n479: \\t// customers) to be able to leverage our API. Their users will need to provide an access token,\\n480: \\t// or the website would need to be added to Sourcegraph's CORS allow list in order to be granted\\n481: \\t// cookie/session-based authentication (which is dangerous to expose to untrusted domains.)\\n482: \\tcrossOriginPolicyAPI crossOriginPolicy = \\\"API\\\"\\n483: \\n484: \\t// crossOriginPolicyAssets describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests to\\n485: \\t// static resources as a public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain.\\n486: \\t//\\n487: \\t// This is to be used for static assets served from the /.assets route. For example, using this\\n488: \\t// route, the Phabricator native extension loads styles via the fetch interface.\\n489: \\tcrossOriginPolicyAssets crossOriginPolicy = \\\"assets\\\"\\n490: \\n491: \\t// crossOriginPolicyNever describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests by\\n492: \\t// never allowing them. This makes sense for e.g. routes such as e.g. sign out pages, where\\n493: \\t// cookie based authentication is needed and requests should never come from a domain other than\\n494: \\t// the Sourcegraph instance itself.\\n495: \\t//\\n496: \\t// Important: This only applies to cross-origin requests issued by clients that respect CORS,\\n497: \\t// such as browsers. So for example Code Intelligence /.executors, despite being \\\"an API\\\",\\n498: \\t// should use this policy unless they intend to get cross-origin requests _from browsers_.\\n499: \\tcrossOriginPolicyNever crossOriginPolicy = \\\"never\\\"\\n500: )\\n501: \\n502: // secureHeadersMiddleware adds and checks for HTTP security-related headers.\\n503: //\\n504: // 🚨 SECURITY: This handler is served to all clients, even on private servers to clients who have\\n505: // not authenticated. It must not reveal any sensitive information.\\n506: func secureHeadersMiddleware(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, next http.Handler, policy crossOriginPolicy) http.Handler {\\n507: \\treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\\n508: \\t\\t// headers for security\\n509: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-Content-Type-Options\\\", \\\"nosniff\\\")\\n510: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-XSS-Protection\\\", \\\"1; mode=block\\\")\\n511: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"X-Frame-Options\\\", \\\"DENY\\\")\\n512: \\t\\t// no cache by default\\n513: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Cache-Control\\\", \\\"no-cache, max-age=0\\\")\\n514: \\n515: \\t\\t// Write CORS headers and potentially handle the requests if it is an OPTIONS request.\\n516: \\t\\tif handled := handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin(logger, db), w, r, policy); handled {\\n517: \\t\\t\\treturn // request was handled, do not invoke next handler\\n518: \\t\\t}\\n519: \\n520: \\t\\tnext.ServeHTTP(w, r)\\n521: \\t})\\n522: }\\n523: \\n524: // handleCORSRequest handles checking the Origin header and writing CORS Access-Control-Allow-*\\n525: // headers. In some cases, it may handle OPTIONS CORS preflight requests in which case the function\\n526: // returns true and the request should be considered fully served.\\n527: func handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin func(context.Context, string) bool, w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request, policy crossOriginPolicy) (handled bool) {\\n528: \\t// If this route is one which should never allow cross-origin requests, then we should return\\n529: \\t// early. We do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browsers\\n530: \\t// default (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\\n531: \\t//\\n532: \\t// We could instead parse the domain from conf.Get().ExternalURL and use that in the response,\\n533: \\t// to make things more explicit, but it would add more logic here to think about and you would\\n534: \\t// also want to think about whether or not `OPTIONS` requests should be handled and if the other\\n535: \\t// headers (-Credentials, -Methods, -Headers, etc.) should be sent back in such a situation.\\n536: \\t// Instead, it's easier to reason about the code by just saying \\\"we send back nothing in this\\n537: \\t// case, and so the browser enforces no cross-origin requests\\\".\\n538: \\t//\\n539: \\t// This is in compliance with section 7.2 \\\"Resource Sharing Check\\\" of the CORS standard: https://www.w3.org/TR/2020/SPSD-cors-20200602/#resource-sharing-check-0\\n540: \\t// It states:\\n541: \\t//\\n542: \\t// > If the response includes zero or more than one Access-Control-Allow-Origin header values,\\n543: \\t// > return fail and terminate this algorithm.\\n544: \\t//\\n545: \\t// And you may also see the type of error the browser would produce in this instance at e.g.\\n546: \\t// https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Errors/CORSMissingAllowOrigin\\n547: \\t//\\n548: \\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyNever {\\n549: \\t\\treturn false\\n550: \\t}\\n551: \\n552: \\t// If the crossOriginPolicyAssets is used and the requested asset is not from the extension folder,\\n553: \\t// we do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browser's default\\n554: \\t// (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\\n555: \\t//\\n556: \\t// We allow cross-origin requests for assets in the `./client/web/dist/extension` folder because they\\n557: \\t// are required for the native Phabricator extension.\\n558: \\tif policy == crossOriginPolicyAssets && !strings.HasPrefix(r.URL.Path, \\\"/extension/\\\") {\\n559: \\t\\treturn false\\n560: \\t}\\n561: \\n562: \\t// Check Fetch metadata to determine request site, if the request is cross-site\\n563: \\t// or the metadata doesn't exist we handle the request.\\n564: \\tif reqSite := r.Header.Get(csrf.SecFetchSite); reqSite != \\\"\\\" && reqSite != \\\"cross-site\\\" {\\n565: \\t\\treturn false\\n566: \\t}\\n567: \\t// crossOriginPolicyAPI and crossOriginPolicyAssets - handling of API and static assets routes.\\n568: \\t//\\n569: \\t// Even if the request was not from a trusted origin, we will allow the browser to send it AND\\n570: \\t// include credentials even. Traditionally, this would be a CSRF vulnerability! But because we\\n571: \\t// know for a fact that we will only respect sessions (cookie-based-authentication) iff the\\n572: \\t// request came from a trusted origin, in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety, we know it\\n573: \\t// is safe to do this.\\n574: \\t//\\n575: \\t// This is the ONLY way in which we can enable public access of our Sourcegraph.com API, i.e. to\\n576: \\t// allow random.com to send requests to our GraphQL and search APIs either unauthenticated or\\n577: \\t// using an access token.\\n578: \\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Credentials\\\", \\\"true\\\")\\n579: \\n580: \\t// Note: This must mirror the request's `Origin` header exactly as API users rely on this\\n581: \\t// codepath handling for example wildcards `*` and `null` origins properly. For example, if\\n582: \\t// Sourcegraph is behind a corporate VPN an admin may choose to set the CORS origin to \\\"*\\\" (via\\n583: \\t// a proxy, a browser would never send a literal \\\"*\\\") and would expect Sourcegraph to respond\\n584: \\t// appropriately with the request's Origin header. Similarly, some environments issue requests\\n585: \\t// with a `null` Origin header, such as VS Code extensions from within WebViews and Figma\\n586: \\t// extensions. Thus:\\n587: \\t//\\n588: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: *\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\\\"\\n589: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: null\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: null\\\"\\n590: \\t// \\t\\\"Origin: https://foobar.com\\\" -> \\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://foobar.com\\\"\\n591: \\t//\\n592: \\t// Again, this is fine because we allow API requests from any origin and instead prevent CSRF\\n593: \\t// attacks via enforcing that we only respect session auth iff the origin is trusted. See the\\n594: \\t// docstring above this one for more info.\\n595: \\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin\\\", r.Header.Get(\\\"Origin\\\"))\\n596: \\n597: \\tif r.Method == \\\"OPTIONS\\\" {\\n598: \\t\\t// CRITICAL: Only trusted origins are allowed to send the secure X-Requested-With and\\n599: \\t\\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client headers, which indicate to us later (in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety)\\n600: \\t\\t// that the request came from a trusted origin. To understand these secure headers, see\\n601: \\t\\t// \\\"What does X-Requested-With do anyway?\\\" in https://github.com/sourcegraph/sourcegraph-public-snapshot/pull/27931\\n602: \\t\\t//\\n603: \\t\\t// Any origin may send us POST, GET, OPTIONS requests with arbitrary content types, auth\\n604: \\t\\t// (session cookies and access tokens), etc. but only trusted origins may send us the secure\\n605: \\t\\t// X-Requested-With header.\\n606: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Methods\\\", \\\"GET, POST, OPTIONS\\\")\\n607: \\n608: \\t\\theaders := []string{}\\n609: \\n610: \\t\\tif isTrustedOrigin(r.Context(), r.Header.Get(\\\"Origin\\\")) {\\n611: \\t\\t\\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client is the deprecated form of X-Requested-With, so we treat it the same\\n612: \\t\\t\\t// way. It is NOT respected anymore, but is left as an allowed header so as to not block\\n613: \\t\\t\\t// requests that still do include it as e.g. part of a proxy put in front of Sourcegraph.\\n614: \\t\\t\\theaders = append(headers, corsAllowHeader, \\\"X-Sourcegraph-Client\\\")\\n615: \\t\\t}\\n616: \\n617: \\t\\t// Add headers specified by the site config. The site must be deployed behind a proxy which\\n618: \\t\\t// manages its auth headers.\\n619: \\t\\tif conf := conf.Get(); conf != nil && conf.AuthProviders != nil {\\n620: \\t\\t\\tfor _, p := range conf.AuthProviders {\\n621: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Add headers specified by the HTTP header auth provider.\\n622: \\t\\t\\t\\tif p.HttpHeader != nil {\\n623: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader != \\\"\\\" {\\n624: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader)\\n625: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n626: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader != \\\"\\\" {\\n627: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader)\\n628: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n629: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n630: \\t\\t\\t}\\n631: \\t\\t}\\n632: \\n633: \\t\\t// safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins is a list of headers that are safe to allow\\n634: \\t\\t// even from untrusted clients. Importantly, this list does _not_ include\\n635: \\t\\t// corsAllowHeader. The list is formatted for use with Access-Control-Allow-Headers.\\n636: \\t\\t//\\n637: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace: indicates whether we should enable tracing for the request\\n638: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name: contains a client-reported name for the request source. Used for event metadata.\\n639: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version: contains a client-reported version for the request source. Used for event metadata.\\n640: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature: contains a client reported feature for the request source. Used for event metadata.\\n641: \\t\\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID: reports an anonymous ID for clients that are not logged in. Used for event metadata unauthed dotcom users.\\n642: \\t\\tconst safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins = \\\"Content-Type, Authorization, X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature, X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID\\\"\\n643: \\t\\theaders = append(headers, safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins)\\n644: \\n645: \\t\\tw.Header().Set(\\\"Access-Control-Allow-Headers\\\", strings.Join(headers, \\\", \\\"))\\n646: \\t\\tw.WriteHeader(http.StatusOK)\\n647: \\t\\treturn true // we handled the request\\n648: \\t}\\n649: \\treturn false\\n650: }\\n651: \\n652: // isTrustedOrigin returns whether the HTTP request's Origin is trusted to\\n653: // initiate authenticated cross-origin requests.\\n654: func newInternalHTTPHandler(\n432: \tschema *graphql.Schema,\n433: \tdb database.DB,\n434: \tgitserverClient gitserver.Client,\n435: \tnewCodeIntelUploadHandler enterprise.NewCodeIntelUploadHandler,\n436: h)\n458: \treturn h\n459: }\n460: \n461: // corsAllowHeader is the HTTP header that, if present (and assuming secureHeadersMiddleware is\n462: // used), indicates that the incoming HTTP request is either same-origin or is from an allowed\n463: // origin. See\n464: // https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Cross-Site_Request_Forgery_(CSRF)_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet#Protecting_REST_Services:_Use_of_Custom_Request_Headers\n465: // for more information on this technique.\n466: const corsAllowHeader = \"X-Requested-With\"\n467: \n468: // crossOriginPolicy describes the cross-origin policy the middleware should be enforcing.\n469: type crossOriginPolicy string\n470: \n471: const (\n472: \t// crossOriginPolicyAPI describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests as a\n473: \t// public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain but\n474: \t// cookie/session-based authentication is only allowed if the origin is in the configured\n475: \t// allow-list of origins. Otherwise, only access token authentication is permitted.\n476: \t//\n477: \t// This is to be used for all /.api routes, such as our GraphQL and search streaming APIs as we\n478: \t// want third-party websites (such as e.g. github1s.com, or internal tools for on-prem\n479: \t// customers) to be able to leverage our API. Their users will need to provide an access token,\n480: \t// or the website would need to be added to Sourcegraph's CORS allow list in order to be granted\n481: \t// cookie/session-based authentication (which is dangerous to expose to untrusted domains.)\n482: \tcrossOriginPolicyAPI crossOriginPolicy = \"API\"\n483: \n484: \t// crossOriginPolicyAssets describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests to\n485: \t// static resources as a public API. That is, cross-origin requests are allowed from any domain.\n486: \t//\n487: \t// This is to be used for static assets served from the /.assets route. For example, using this\n488: \t// route, the Phabricator native extension loads styles via the fetch interface.\n489: \tcrossOriginPolicyAssets crossOriginPolicy = \"assets\"\n490: \n491: \t// crossOriginPolicyNever describes that the middleware should handle cross-origin requests by\n492: \t// never allowing them. This makes sense for e.g. routes such as e.g. sign out pages, where\n493: \t// cookie based authentication is needed and requests should never come from a domain other than\n494: \t// the Sourcegraph instance itself.\n495: \t//\n496: \t// Important: This only applies to cross-origin requests issued by clients that respect CORS,\n497: \t// such as browsers. So for example Code Intelligence /.executors, despite being \"an API\",\n498: \t// should use this policy unless they intend to get cross-origin requests _from browsers_.\n499: \tcrossOriginPolicyNever crossOriginPolicy = \"never\"\n500: )\n501: \n502: // secureHeadersMiddleware adds and checks for HTTP security-related headers.\n503: //\n504: // 🚨 SECURITY: This handler is served to all clients, even on private servers to clients who have\n505: // not authenticated. It must not reveal any sensitive information.\n506: func secureHeadersMiddleware(logger log.Logger, db database.DB, next http.Handler, policy crossOriginPolicy) http.Handler {\n507: \treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n508: \t\t// headers for security\n509: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Content-Type-Options\", \"nosniff\")\n510: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-XSS-Protection\", \"1; mode=block\")\n511: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"X-Frame-Options\", \"DENY\")\n512: \t\t// no cache by default\n513: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"Cache-Control\", \"no-cache, max-age=0\")\n514: \n515: \t\t// Write CORS headers and potentially handle the requests if it is an OPTIONS request.\n516: \t\tif handled := handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin(logger, db), w, r, policy); handled {\n517: \t\t\treturn // request was handled, do not invoke next handler\n518: \t\t}\n519: \n520: \t\tnext.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n521: \t})\n522: }\n523: \n524: // handleCORSRequest handles checking the Origin header and writing CORS Access-Control-Allow-*\n525: // headers. In some cases, it may handle OPTIONS CORS preflight requests in which case the function\n526: // returns true and the request should be considered fully served.\n527: func handleCORSRequest(isTrustedOrigin func(context.Context, string) bool, w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request, policy crossOriginPolicy) (handled bool) {\n528: \t// If this route is one which should never allow cross-origin requests, then we should return\n529: \t// early. We do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browsers\n530: \t// default (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n531: \t//\n532: \t// We could instead parse the domain from conf.Get().ExternalURL and use that in the response,\n533: \t// to make things more explicit, but it would add more logic here to think about and you would\n534: \t// also want to think about whether or not `OPTIONS` requests should be handled and if the other\n535: \t// headers (-Credentials, -Methods, -Headers, etc.) should be sent back in such a situation.\n536: \t// Instead, it's easier to reason about the code by just saying \"we send back nothing in this\n537: \t// case, and so the browser enforces no cross-origin requests\".\n538: \t//\n539: \t// This is in compliance with section 7.2 \"Resource Sharing Check\" of the CORS standard: https://www.w3.org/TR/2020/SPSD-cors-20200602/#resource-sharing-check-0\n540: \t// It states:\n541: \t//\n542: \t// > If the response includes zero or more than one Access-Control-Allow-Origin header values,\n543: \t// > return fail and terminate this algorithm.\n544: \t//\n545: \t// And you may also see the type of error the browser would produce in this instance at e.g.\n546: \t// https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Errors/CORSMissingAllowOrigin\n547: \t//\n548: \tif policy == crossOriginPolicyNever {\n549: \t\treturn false\n550: \t}\n551: \n552: \t// If the crossOriginPolicyAssets is used and the requested asset is not from the extension folder,\n553: \t// we do not write ANY Access-Control-Allow-* CORS headers, which triggers the browser's default\n554: \t// (and strict) behavior of not allowing cross-origin requests.\n555: \t//\n556: \t// We allow cross-origin requests for assets in the `./client/web/dist/extension` folder because they\n557: \t// are required for the native Phabricator extension.\n558: \tif policy == crossOriginPolicyAssets && !strings.HasPrefix(r.URL.Path, \"/extension/\") {\n559: \t\treturn false\n560: \t}\n561: \n562: \t// Check Fetch metadata to determine request site, if the request is cross-site\n563: \t// or the metadata doesn't exist we handle the request.\n564: \tif reqSite := r.Header.Get(csrf.SecFetchSite); reqSite != \"\" && reqSite != \"cross-site\" {\n565: \t\treturn false\n566: \t}\n567: \t// crossOriginPolicyAPI and crossOriginPolicyAssets - handling of API and static assets routes.\n568: \t//\n569: \t// Even if the request was not from a trusted origin, we will allow the browser to send it AND\n570: \t// include credentials even. Traditionally, this would be a CSRF vulnerability! But because we\n571: \t// know for a fact that we will only respect sessions (cookie-based-authentication) iff the\n572: \t// request came from a trusted origin, in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety, we know it\n573: \t// is safe to do this.\n574: \t//\n575: \t// This is the ONLY way in which we can enable public access of our Sourcegraph.com API, i.e. to\n576: \t// allow random.com to send requests to our GraphQL and search APIs either unauthenticated or\n577: \t// using an access token.\n578: \tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Credentials\", \"true\")\n579: \n580: \t// Note: This must mirror the request's `Origin` header exactly as API users rely on this\n581: \t// codepath handling for example wildcards `*` and `null` origins properly. For example, if\n582: \t// Sourcegraph is behind a corporate VPN an admin may choose to set the CORS origin to \"*\" (via\n583: \t// a proxy, a browser would never send a literal \"*\") and would expect Sourcegraph to respond\n584: \t// appropriately with the request's Origin header. Similarly, some environments issue requests\n585: \t// with a `null` Origin header, such as VS Code extensions from within WebViews and Figma\n586: \t// extensions. Thus:\n587: \t//\n588: \t// \t\"Origin: *\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\"\n589: \t// \t\"Origin: null\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: null\"\n590: \t// \t\"Origin: https://foobar.com\" -> \"Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://foobar.com\"\n591: \t//\n592: \t// Again, this is fine because we allow API requests from any origin and instead prevent CSRF\n593: \t// attacks via enforcing that we only respect session auth iff the origin is trusted. See the\n594: \t// docstring above this one for more info.\n595: \tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Origin\", r.Header.Get(\"Origin\"))\n596: \n597: \tif r.Method == \"OPTIONS\" {\n598: \t\t// CRITICAL: Only trusted origins are allowed to send the secure X-Requested-With and\n599: \t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client headers, which indicate to us later (in session.go:CookieMiddlewareWIthCSRFSafety)\n600: \t\t// that the request came from a trusted origin. To understand these secure headers, see\n601: \t\t// \"What does X-Requested-With do anyway?\" in https://github.com/sourcegraph/sourcegraph-public-snapshot/pull/27931\n602: \t\t//\n603: \t\t// Any origin may send us POST, GET, OPTIONS requests with arbitrary content types, auth\n604: \t\t// (session cookies and access tokens), etc. but only trusted origins may send us the secure\n605: \t\t// X-Requested-With header.\n606: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Methods\", \"GET, POST, OPTIONS\")\n607: \n608: \t\theaders := []string{}\n609: \n610: \t\tif isTrustedOrigin(r.Context(), r.Header.Get(\"Origin\")) {\n611: \t\t\t// X-Sourcegraph-Client is the deprecated form of X-Requested-With, so we treat it the same\n612: \t\t\t// way. It is NOT respected anymore, but is left as an allowed header so as to not block\n613: \t\t\t// requests that still do include it as e.g. part of a proxy put in front of Sourcegraph.\n614: \t\t\theaders = append(headers, corsAllowHeader, \"X-Sourcegraph-Client\")\n615: \t\t}\n616: \n617: \t\t// Add headers specified by the site config. The site must be deployed behind a proxy which\n618: \t\t// manages its auth headers.\n619: \t\tif conf := conf.Get(); conf != nil && conf.AuthProviders != nil {\n620: \t\t\tfor _, p := range conf.AuthProviders {\n621: \t\t\t\t// Add headers specified by the HTTP header auth provider.\n622: \t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader != nil {\n623: \t\t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader != \"\" {\n624: \t\t\t\t\t\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.EmailHeader)\n625: \t\t\t\t\t}\n626: \t\t\t\t\tif p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader != \"\" {\n627: \t\t\t\t\t\theaders = append(headers, p.HttpHeader.UsernameHeader)\n628: \t\t\t\t\t}\n629: \t\t\t\t}\n630: \t\t\t}\n631: \t\t}\n632: \n633: \t\t// safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins is a list of headers that are safe to allow\n634: \t\t// even from untrusted clients. Importantly, this list does _not_ include\n635: \t\t// corsAllowHeader. The list is formatted for use with Access-Control-Allow-Headers.\n636: \t\t//\n637: \t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace: indicates whether we should enable tracing for the request\n638: \t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name: contains a client-reported name for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n639: \t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version: contains a client-reported version for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n640: \t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature: contains a client reported feature for the request source. Used for event metadata.\n641: \t\t// - X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID: reports an anonymous ID for clients that are not logged in. Used for event metadata unauthed dotcom users.\n642: \t\tconst safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins = \"Content-Type, Authorization, X-Sourcegraph-Should-Trace, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Name, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Version, X-Sourcegraph-API-Client-Feature, X-Sourcegraph-Actor-Anonymous-UID\"\n643: \t\theaders = append(headers, safeHeadersForUntrustedOrigins)\n644: \n645: \t\tw.Header().Set(\"Access-Control-Allow-Headers\", strings.Join(headers, \", \"))\n646: \t\tw.WriteHeader(http.StatusOK)\n647: \t\treturn true // we handled the request\n648: \t}\n649: \treturn false\n650: }\n651: \n652: // isTrustedOrigin returns whether the HTTP request's Origin is trusted to\n653: // initiate authenticated cross-origin requests.\n654: func isTrustedOrigin(logger log.Logger, db database.DB) func(ctx context.Context, requestOrigin string) bool {\n655: \treturn func(ctx context.Context, requestOrigin string) bool {\n656: \t\tisExtensionRequest := requestOrigin == devExtension || requestOrigin == prodExtension\n657: \n658: \t\tvar isCORSAllowedRequest bool\n659: \t\tif corsOrigin := conf.Get().CorsOrigin; corsOrigin != \"\" {\n660: \t\t\tisCORSAllowedRequest = isAllowedOrigin(requestOrigin, strings.Fields(corsOrigin))\n661: \t\t}\n662: \n663: \t\textURL, err := db.Conf().GetExternalURL(ctx)\n664: \t\tif err != nil {\n665: \t\t\tlogger.Error(\"failed to get external URL\", log.Error(err))\n666: \t\t\treturn false\n667: \t\t}\n668: \n669: \t\tif externalURL := strings.TrimSuffix(extURL.String(), \"/\"); externalURL != \"\" && requestOrigin == externalURL {\n670: \t\t\tisCORSAllowedRequest = true\n671: \t\t}\n672: \n673: \t\treturn isExtensionRequest || isCORSAllowedRequest\n674: \t}\n675: }\n676: \n677: func newDeepSearchAgent(\n678: \tdb database.DB,\n679: \tgp gating.Provider,\n680: \thandlers *httpapi.Handlers,\n681: \tlogger log.Logger,\n682: ) deepsearchapi.DeepSearchAgent {\n683: \tdeepSearchChatClient := llmutils.NewChatClientFromInternalCompletions(\n684: \t\tsync.OnceValue(func() completions.InternalCompletionsService {\n685: \t\t\treturn handlers.DeepSearchCompletionsService\n686: \t\t}),\n687: \t)\n688: \tgitserverClient := gitserver.NewClient(\"deepsearch\")\n689: \tsearchClient := searchclient.New(logger, db, gitserverClient, search.SourceDeepSearch)\n690: \ttoolRegistry := tools.CreateToolRegistry(tools.ModeDeepSearch, logger.Scoped(\"deepsearch.tools\"), db, gitserverClient, searchClient, handlers.CodeNavResolver, deepSearchChatClient)\n691: \tsuggester := suggestions.NewSuggester(deepSearchChatClient)\n692: \n693: \tworkerPool := deepsearchapi.NewWorkerPool(deepsearch.DefaultNumWorkers, logger)\n694: \ttelemetryEventRecorder := telemetryrecorder.New(db)\n695: \teventBroker := deepsearchapi.NewRedisBroker(logger.Scoped(\"deepsearch.broker\"), redispool.Store)\n696: \n697: \treturn deepsearchapi.NewDeepsearchAgent(db, gp,\n698: \t\tlogger.Scoped(\"deepsearch.agent\"),\n699: \t\ttelemetryEventRecorder,\n700: \t\tdeepSearchChatClient,\n701: \t\ttoolRegistry,\n702: \t\tsuggester,\n703: \t\tworkerPool,\n704: \t\teventBroker,\n705: \t)\n706: }\n707: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sourcegraph/sourcegraph@2182d53b963752f43e9f39205715f71160798bb2/-/blob/cmd/frontend/internal/cli/http.go"}}}

The outermost layers (first to run) handle infrastructure concerns: IP allowlist enforcement (ipallowlist), tenant resolution from hostname (multi-tenant cloud), distributed tracing (instrumentation, trace), anonymous UID tracking (session.AnonymousUIDMiddleware), and request client info extraction (requestclient). CORS and security headers are applied per-route via secureHeadersMiddleware.\\n\\nAuthentication credential extraction runs next, applied bottom-up (LIFO order in code): (1) HTTP Header Auth (httpheader.AuthMiddleware) for proxy-based auth where a trusted upstream proxy sets a username/email header; (2) Access Token Auth (accesstoken.AccessTokenAuthMiddleware) which accepts tokens via query param, Basic Auth, or 'Authorization: token <tok>' header — supports sudo tokens for site admins; (3) OAuth Token Auth (oauthtoken.OAuthTokenAuthMiddleware) for tokens issued by the internal IdP (Fosite-based). For the GraphQL/internal API, cookie/session auth is then checked via session.CookieMiddlewareWithCSRFSafety (CSRF-safe: only trusts cookies from trusted origins identified by Sec-Fetch-Site and Origin headers); for the App (HTML), session.CookieMiddleware is used unconditionally. Sessions are stored in Redis (gorilla/sessions + redistore).\\n\\nAfter credentials are extracted the actor is set in context. Auth enforcement follows: APIRequireAuthMiddleware / AppRequireAuthMiddleware / ExternalAPIRequireAuthMiddleware reject unauthenticated requests for protected routes (allowAnonymousRequest defines the exempted paths such as sign-in, webhooks, LSIF uploads). API scope enforcement (apiscope.RequireScopes) then validates that access tokens carry the required scopes (user:all or mcp scopes). Feature flags are injected (featureflag.Middleware). Finally, authz.PostAuthMiddleware enforces licensing — authenticated non-admin users are blocked if the Sourcegraph license/grant is invalid.\\n\\nAuthN providers register via providers.RegisterProviderFactory during Init(): builtin username/password (userpasswd), GitHub OAuth (githuboauth), GitLab OAuth (gitlaboauth), Azure DevOps OAuth (azureoauth), Bitbucket Cloud OAuth (bitbucketcloudoauth), Bitbucket Server OAuth (bitbucketserveroauth), Gerrit (gerrit), HTTP Header (httpheader), OpenID Connect (oidc), SAML 2.0 (saml), Sourcegraph Operator/SOAP (sourcegraphoperator), and Sourcegraph Accounts/SAMS (sourcegraphaccounts). Auth flow endpoints are served under /.auth/ via dedicated handlers (SOAP login/callback, SAML metadata/login/ACS/logout, OIDC login/callback, generic OAuth login/callback). The ConnectOrSignOutMiddleware on /.auth/ handles session sign-out vs account connection flows.\\n\\nRepository-level authorization is enforced via the authz.Provider interface (internal/authz/iface.go) implemented by 7 code-host providers: GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket Server, Bitbucket Cloud, Gerrit, Azure DevOps, and Perforce. These are instantiated by NewAuthzProviderFactory (internal/authz/providers/authz.go) which reads external service configs. Permissions are synced to the database by a background worker (cmd/worker/internal/authz/perms_syncer.go) and enforced in SQL queries via AuthzQueryConds (internal/database/permdb/repos_perm.go) which filters the repo table against the user_repo_permissions table. Sub-repository permissions (file-level ACLs) are handled via the SubRepoPermissionChecker interface. The external connect API (externalapi) uses an additional authz interceptor (externalapi/middleware/authz.go) for Connect/gRPC endpoints.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":10659,"cache_read_input_tokens":66111,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":10659,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"87c872ea-1898-40bb-8b85-68d250628546","uuid":"0a75592a-3692-4017-bad2-f9451b1c629c"}

Middleware runs outermost-first (innermost registered last in LIFO stacking). Global layers applied to every request: (1) IP allowlist (ipallowlist) blocks forbidden IPs immediately; (2) tenant resolution from hostname (multi-tenant cloud); (3) instrumentation/tracing (instrumentation.HTTPMiddleware, tracepkg.HTTPMiddleware); (4) requestclient extraction from HTTP headers; (5) anonymous UID from cookie (session.AnonymousUIDMiddleware) for analytics; (6) CORS + security headers (secureHeadersMiddleware) which also enforces origin trust.\\n\\nCredential extraction middleware (applied per route handler, LIFO — last line runs first): (a) httpheader.AuthMiddleware — reads a configured proxy-set header (e.g. X-Forwarded-User) and sets the actor from a trusted upstream auth proxy; (b) accesstoken.AccessTokenAuthMiddleware — validates Sourcegraph personal access tokens from query param, Basic Auth, or 'Authorization: token <tok>' header, supports sudo impersonation for site admins, attaches API scopes to context; (c) oauthtoken.OAuthTokenAuthMiddleware — validates OAuth 2.0 Bearer tokens issued by the internal Fosite-based IdP (served at /.auth/idp/oauth/*); (d) session.CookieMiddlewareWithCSRFSafety (API) or session.CookieMiddleware (App) — reads gorilla/sessions Redis-backed session cookie, enforces CSRF safety by only trusting cookies from same-origin or allow-listed CORS origins (checked via Sec-Fetch-Site header + Origin fallback).\\n\\nAuth enforcement: APIRequireAuthMiddleware / AppRequireAuthMiddleware / ExternalAPIRequireAuthMiddleware reject unauthenticated requests unless AllowAnonymousRequest permits the path (sign-in pages, webhooks, LSIF/SCIP upload endpoints). ConnectOrSignOutMiddleware on /.auth/ decides whether to connect an external account or sign out. apiscope.RequireScopes enforces that access tokens carry required scopes (user:all for API/App, mcp scope for MCP paths). featureflag.Middleware adds feature flags to context. authz.PostAuthMiddleware enforces license validity — blocks non-admin authenticated users when the Sourcegraph license/grant is invalid.\\n\\nAuth provider registration: auth.Init() (cmd/frontend/internal/auth/init.go) initialises 12 providers, each calling providers.RegisterProviderFactory: builtin username/password (userpasswd), GitHub OAuth (githuboauth), GitLab OAuth (gitlaboauth), Azure DevOps OAuth (azureoauth), Bitbucket Cloud OAuth (bitbucketcloudoauth), Bitbucket Server OAuth (bitbucketserveroauth), Gerrit (gerrit), HTTP Header proxy (httpheader), OpenID Connect (oidc), SAML 2.0 (saml), Sourcegraph Operator/SOAP (sourcegraphoperator), and Sourcegraph Accounts/SAMS (sourcegraphaccounts). Auth flow endpoints are mounted at /.auth/ and dispatch to typed handlers (SOAP login+callback, SAML metadata/login/ACS/logout, OIDC login/callback, generic OAuth login/callback, authvalidation). Sessions are created/updated in these callbacks and stored in Redis.\\n\\nRepository-level authorization uses the authz.Provider interface (internal/authz/iface.go) with methods FetchUserPerms, FetchRepoPerms, and FetchAccount. Seven code-host authz providers are instantiated by NewAuthzProviderFactory (internal/authz/providers/authz.go): GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket Server, Bitbucket Cloud, Gerrit, Azure DevOps, and Perforce. Permissions are synced to the database by a background worker (cmd/worker/internal/authz/perms_syncer.go) and enforced in SQL via AuthzQueryConds (internal/database/permdb/repos_perm.go) which joins against the user_repo_permissions table. Sub-repository file-level permissions are gated via SubRepoPermissionChecker (internal/authz/sub_repo_perms.go). The external Connect/gRPC API has an additional per-method authz interceptor (externalapi/middleware/authz.go) that checks proto method options against the actor's roles.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":374,"cache_read_input_tokens":83688,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":374,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"87c872ea-1898-40bb-8b85-68d250628546","uuid":"53f243f7-e80a-4857-918c-d01fb7d766a6"}

],\n  \"summary\": \"Sourcegraph's frontend auth chain is assembled in newExternalHTTPHandler (cmd/frontend/internal/cli/http.go). Middleware runs outermost-first (innermost registered last in LIFO stacking). Global layers applied to every request: (1) IP allowlist (ipallowlist) blocks forbidden IPs immediately; (2) tenant resolution from hostname (multi-tenant cloud); (3) instrumentation/tracing (instrumentation.HTTPMiddleware, tracepkg.HTTPMiddleware); (4) requestclient extraction from HTTP headers; (5) anonymous UID from cookie (session.AnonymousUIDMiddleware) for analytics; (6) CORS + security headers (secureHeadersMiddleware) which also enforces origin trust.\\n\\nCredential extraction middleware (applied per route handler, LIFO — last line runs first): (a) httpheader.AuthMiddleware — reads a configured proxy-set header (e.g. X-Forwarded-User) and sets the actor from a trusted upstream auth proxy; (b) accesstoken.AccessTokenAuthMiddleware — validates Sourcegraph personal access tokens from query param, Basic Auth, or 'Authorization: token <tok>' header, supports sudo impersonation for site admins, attaches API scopes to context; (c) oauthtoken.OAuthTokenAuthMiddleware — validates OAuth 2.0 Bearer tokens issued by the internal Fosite-based IdP (served at /.auth/idp/oauth/*); (d) session.CookieMiddlewareWithCSRFSafety (API) or session.CookieMiddleware (App) — reads gorilla/sessions Redis-backed session cookie, enforces CSRF safety by only trusting cookies from same-origin or allow-listed CORS origins (checked via Sec-Fetch-Site header + Origin fallback).\\n\\nAuth enforcement: APIRequireAuthMiddleware / AppRequireAuthMiddleware / ExternalAPIRequireAuthMiddleware reject unauthenticated requests unless AllowAnonymousRequest permits the path (sign-in pages, webhooks, LSIF/SCIP upload endpoints). ConnectOrSignOutMiddleware on /.auth/ decides whether to connect an external account or sign out. apiscope.RequireScopes enforces that access tokens carry required scopes (user:all for API/App, mcp scope for MCP paths). featureflag.Middleware adds feature flags to context. authz.PostAuthMiddleware enforces license validity — blocks non-admin authenticated users when the Sourcegraph license/grant is invalid.\\n\\nAuth provider registration: auth.Init() (cmd/frontend/internal/auth/init.go) initialises 12 providers, each calling providers.RegisterProviderFactory: builtin username/password (userpasswd), GitHub OAuth (githuboauth), GitLab OAuth (gitlaboauth), Azure DevOps OAuth (azureoauth), Bitbucket Cloud OAuth (bitbucketcloudoauth), Bitbucket Server OAuth (bitbucketserveroauth), Gerrit (gerrit), HTTP Header proxy (httpheader), OpenID Connect (oidc), SAML 2.0 (saml), Sourcegraph Operator/SOAP (sourcegraphoperator), and Sourcegraph Accounts/SAMS (sourcegraphaccounts). Auth flow endpoints are mounted at /.auth/ and dispatch to typed handlers (SOAP login+callback, SAML metadata/login/ACS/logout, OIDC login/callback, generic OAuth login/callback, authvalidation). Sessions are created/updated in these callbacks and stored in Redis.\\n\\nRepository-level authorization uses the authz.Provider interface (internal/authz/iface.go) with methods FetchUserPerms, FetchRepoPerms, and FetchAccount. Seven code-host authz providers are instantiated by NewAuthzProviderFactory (internal/authz/providers/authz.go): GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket Server, Bitbucket Cloud, Gerrit, Azure DevOps, and Perforce. Permissions are synced to the database by a background worker (cmd/worker/internal/authz/perms_syncer.go) and enforced in SQL via AuthzQueryConds (internal/database/permdb/repos_perm.go) which joins against the user_repo_permissions table. Sub-repository file-level permissions are gated via SubRepoPermissionChecker (internal/authz/sub_repo_perms.go). The external Connect/gRPC API has an additional per-method authz interceptor (externalapi/middleware/authz.go) that checks proto method options against the actor's roles.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
